< text>
Dont normally write reviews but this place deserves the time it takes. The staff went way above and beyond in helping us. It's late in the season and I can not find snow pants anywhere. I called this place just in hope that I can find something before my trip to Tahoe. The very nice woman went over what sizes they had and price points to get an idea over the phone. I showed up about 2 hours later for her to greet me at the door and asked if I was the man who called. She then preceded to show me a whole assortment of different sizes and colors she had hand picked out before I got there so it would make my shopping experience easy. She went way above and beyond. Customer service at this place is an easy 5 out of 5 stars and the knowledge of their products was unmatched by anywhere iv been before. Thank you Helm of Sun Valley!< /text>

< Review>
Overall good experience, but this shop did not earn 5 stars. I love supporting small businesses, and I love mom-and-pop shops, especially when it comes to skiing; however, their service was sub par, and that seems essential since they're inventory is not what you can find at other ski shops. I was happy with the repair they performed on my skis, and if you need work done I would recommend them but only if you don't have a deadline for when you want the skis back.  They were a better deal on the repairs I needed then the local REI and many other local ski shops. Additionally, one of the hallmarks of a great ski shop is their willingness to work as an interface between the industry and the customer, and they seemed completely uninterested in helping out.  So, only 4 stars from me, I would go back, but I will keep searching for another shop. The buck didn't stop here.<//Review>

< review>
Why 4 stars? Because it's quick, cheap and convenient.

---   ---   ---

This is one of the closest physical eateries to my office when I'm in SF, so it was only a matter of time before I tried it out. And when I see a prosciutto and mozzarella sandwich on any menu, it's very unlikely that I am going to choose anything besides that.

I've certainly had better prosciutto and mozzarella sandwiches before, but I enjoyed it. What I enjoyed even more was that it was probably less from 100 steps from office to sandwich and that it came in at $16.91 for the sammy + chips and a drink. In SF, that's a super cheap lunch.

I'm sure I will be back many times during future work lunches.<//review>

I have started coming here more often now that I realized it is significantly cheaper than most places nearby. The staff seem pretty friendly but I don't know them by name yet.
I have also found that the breakfast bagels from here seem a lot more fresh than other places. They aren't microwaved.
The breakfast bagel I had was decent. There is a pretty large menu however and I will try something else next time to see if I can find something amazing. The mocha I ordered was pretty tasty. The establishment is pretty small with just two tiny tables so chances are you will have to order to go if you go at lunch or breakfast times.<//Text>

< review>
San Diego County Solar designed and installed our residential solar array system in spring of 2019, and we could not be happier with the results. Ken Roberts was our primary interface with San Diego County Solar, and he could be reached  by phone, text, or email at any stage during the process. Additionally, he was on site for major phases of the installation to coordinate with us any details that needed to be confirmed. This level of personal accessibility and contact with a company representative (Ken) in a project of this scope is invaluable.

We found the San Diego County Solar installation crew to be courteous, respectful,  and professional. We were notified of the scheduled work days and times, and updated as well of any changes due to poor weather. During this period there was a substantial amount of rain, and the crew worked around these delaying obstacles very efficiently. During the installation process we were consulted regarding the placement and locations of outdoor electrical conduits, the  painting of reflective surfaces to match the home colors, and placement of wall mounted components, and all of the installation details fit properly with HOA requirements.

Ken and San Diego County Solar also handled all of the interactions with SDG&E; our participation was limited to logging into our account and, under Ken‚Äôs easy to follow direction, making the required selections in the online portal to switch our account to that of a solar generation customer.   Additionally, Ken and his colleagues managed the fast-tracking application for solar activation that allowed our system go online with SDG&E within one day of the City Permit being approved.

It has been six weeks since our system went on-line, and it is clear that the projections Ken made for the system production levels are accurate and honest; if anything his projections for electricity generation were lower than what we are actually experiencing.

If you are considering a solar installation, we whole heartedly recommend Ken Roberts and San Diego County Solar as the vendor of choice for such a project. We found them to be honest, fair, and conscientious about their work and their relations with their customers.< /review>

So far (only 4 days after PTO) the system is performing above expectations for this time of the year and the meter is spinning backwards as we send some excess power back to the grid each day. I can highly recommend San Diego County Solar, especially if you want a trouble free process of adding solar to your house. Looking forward of years of solar powered electricity.</Text>

<name>Shih-wei Wu</name>< text>
Came here on a holiday in the morning, so the wait was minimal.

The waitress was fantastic, she sat us down with a menu in no time. She really made the experience great for us.

Ramen is good. I am hesitant to call it amazing, but the noodle texture was superb. The broth is solid. I would recommend people to come to this place for a bowl. Perhaps event better after a drunken night at a local bar.

Why one star off?

Skip the yellow fin collar. I ordered it on a whim. I should have known better. This was a Monday on MLk day.  They also clearly stated that it was the last one. It had no flavor and over cooked.</text>

(I ‚Äôm a Japanese, born and raised in Japan.)
For ramen lovers from Fukuoka, it was very difficult to find Japanese ramen in San Diego. Almost all the famous ramen shops in San Diego went, but it was just "Nanchatte American Ramen" ... it wasn't delicious at all. In particular, the noodles were so stretched that I felt it was foolish to pay honestly to eat them. Lol

After eating delicious salt ramen at Ramen Ryoma, ramen is here! I liked the Claremont store because it was easy to stop the car, but did it close? I've only used the Hill Crest store a few times, but the interior is stylish and it doesn't look like a ramen shop.

Ramen Ryoma's salt ramen is a real Japanese ramen. Both the soup and noodles have a Japanese taste and are delicious. I noticed that the Claremont store hasn't opened recently ... Never close the Hill Crest store. (I don't know if there is a Japanese clerk, but w)
